## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) in a chemical reaction as a function of time t and concentration A. The rate law typically depends on concentration raised to some power, but time dependence may indicate complex mechanisms like autocatalysis, sequential reactions, or externally driven reactions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (approach to equilibrium with reverse reaction)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics, saturation kinetics)
- Substrate inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (enzyme kinetics with inhibition)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface-catalyzed reaction)
- Time-dependent decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-modulated rate)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (complex mechanism with baseline)
- Cooperative kinetics (Hill): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding/reaction)
- Parallel pathway: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 * A**c3 (multiple simultaneous reaction pathways)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no explicit t) → classical rate law; the ODE is autonomous, suggesting a well-defined reaction mechanism
- Rational function of A (numerator/denominator polynomials in A) → enzyme or surface catalysis mechanism with adsorption/saturation
- Product of A and (constant - A) → autocatalytic or logistic mechanism where both reactant and product participate
- Negative sign in dA/dt with positive A dependence → reactant consumption; positive sign → product formation or autocatalysis
- Integer power of A (1, 2, 3) → molecularity hints at elementary reaction step; non-integer power → complex/effective mechanism
- Explicit time dependence in rate law → non-autonomous system suggesting external forcing, catalyst deactivation, or photochemical effects
- Square in denominator (1+A)^2 → competitive adsorption on surfaces (Langmuir-Hinshelwood mechanism)
- Sum of power-law terms with different exponents → parallel competing reaction pathways or consecutive elementary steps
